< Text>
ABH is a banquet hall that‚Äôs tucked behind a strip mall right off Van Nuys Blvd. They provide two ballrooms depending on your party size. For our event, we choose Ballroom B that was able to accommodate more than 200 guests.

The ballroom was grand, super tall ceiling, white walls, white draping, and skylights that can be customized to whatever color your party theme is. They provide round tables that fit up to ten guests and chiavari chairs are included. They also have an array of tablecloth and napkin linen colors for you to choose from. There‚Äôs a stage where you can set up a live band or a DJ (use your own or you can use the venue‚Äôs preferred DJ for an additional cost.)

You can choose your own caterer or you can use their preferred vendor. If you opt to use their vendor, it is buffet-style of Menu A: Mexican food (choose up to 4 dishes, 2 sides, and dessert) or Menu B: Italian/American food (choose 2 dishes, 2 sides, and dessert). We choose Menu B and you can even make an appointment to the caterer‚Äôs restaurant to try the food before choosing. Also UNLIMITED soda & ice, and water are INCLUDED!!

My point of contact in arranging the event was Kevin. He was quick to respond to my inquiry and when I met with him in person he was nice and accommodating to my party needs. I was very concise with what I needed for the event and he was very direct & honest - so that there was no need for multiple back & forth communication.

He allows your party to bring your own alcohol but you have to keep it behind the bar area with the bar staff - especially if there are guests under the legal drinking age attending. Or you can use his preferred bar tending vendor.

ABH provides their own security. They were really nice and they opened the door for the guests as they arrived. Ballroom B provides a red carpet entrance. There‚Äôs a valet parking staff that are diligent as well. There‚Äôs also a multiple-stall women‚Äôs bathroom, a small changing room or coat/purse check area, and cool & efficient AC flowing throughout the entire ballroom!

Day of the event was smooth, food came out promptly at the time we scheduled. Guests were happy, eating & dancing merrily away. You would never guess that you were in Panorama City tucked behind a strip mall at all!
Kevin and his staff were great to work with; I have a few more events in the future and Angeleno Banquet Hall is already the venue I have in mind for booking.

Book your next event here, your party planning will be smooth and your event will be fantastic!!< /Text>

<Text>I decided to try out Cornerstone one day a couple of years ago because I had driven by it on the freeway for so many years. I did not know what to expect, other than what I had seen on their website about service times and where it was. The worship was contemporary and fun, and the sermon and pastor were both wonderful. All of the pastors teach from the Bible and have all of the readings from the sermon in our notes, to read along with, highlight and write notes on. The sermon notes also include a fill-in-the-blank type study to follow along with, which reinforces the principles that we just read about, and it really helps me to connect to what I'm reading. In addition, the pastors are the perfect balance of funny, energetic and reverent, which is even better than I had hoped for when I was trying out the church. Everyone at Cornerstone is so friendly, from the moment you get out of your car and every step of the way. I am so happy to say that after 5 years of "church-hopping" looking for the "right" church for me, I found not only that at Cornerstone, but I found a family too. The Bible study groups and ministry departments are such a blessing and I can't recommend this church enough if you live in the area.<//Text>< Resp>

<rate>2< /rate><review>I rarely leave a rating below four or five (check my reviews) but, I think this experience was one I would want others to be aware of before going to this dealer. He has good reviews online so I was led to believe this was a lot that would be professional, negotiable (within reason) and overall positive.  This is of course just my experience, I am not perfect but I do believe I am objective. If interested in saving yourself some time, read on.

While the lot is nice, when it comes down to making a deal he will dismiss or explain away findings of a vehicle inspection (PPI's you buy is normal for Porsches) as well a KBB, NADA, Hagerty Values. He will also gladly allow you to walk on a cash offer difference of 500 dollars, his call of course...its his car. Even when you as the buyer are ok assuming the risk the repair on an oil seal he had done by his friends shop that may be faulty (PPI discovered leak, his shop claims not so after wiping it away and running the car at idle for 15 min). That plus older 2016 tires (tires can be older and still have plenty of tread) he claims were put on in 2017 (doesn't matter when they were put on, just when they were cast) left enough concern to make an offer as I knew I would have to fix/change them. Its not a new car, nothing is perfect and one should not expect them to be but should a buyer and seller consider all factors to come to a final price? You make the call. He seems quite open for the car to sit for as long as it takes and that is certainly his right to do. As he said, he has to make money (we all do) and so he doesn't have to sell the car. My advice, call and get a price locked down with Pat before you go and especially before you pay for an inspection on a car like this (Porsche 996). I made the mistake of presuming we could find middle ground, I was wrong. A shame to drive a distance to have a cash offered potential sale fall apart. In the end after I called 10 days later and my offer to come up and meet in the middle giving 250.00 more was rejected did I finally throw up my hands, no reasoning with them at all. Communication had been pretty good up till I walked on 4/9 when we could not make a deal. He claims later I asked for a "discount" as well. For someone selling cars as long as he has...nobody gives "discounts" or asks for them...this is not a restaurant nor did I clip coupons to make a deal. Negotiation is just part of car buying and using data to come to a reasonable price is a common practice here. With 40+ years in business...they should know this.

In case you are wondering as the reader...I 100% agree...nobody won here, its a shame it didn't work out but for those going to his lot in the future just be prepared to pay whatever he says...ignore the data...he does. He knows best, he will be sure you know that too.  He didn't care about my experience at all either until I left a review, he certainly wanted to cry foul then. Did he in his yelp response or CarGurus want to work it out, say sorry it didn't work out? No, instead they levy baseless accusations and assertions which you should of course read, fair is fair. Accusing someone of "blackmail" for leaving a review? That implies I would remove the review if he accepted my offer, no thanks...far to many read flags say move on. When done ask yourself is that how a professional business acts when taking criticism? Any ownership or responsibility taken on his end? Not even once did he say "lets work this out" or "how can we make this right" like most any business we would do. He has a few other responses to critical reviews like this...all of them I saw...zero...zero effort to resolve with the respondent. Is this who you want to buy from?

In closing, I  would say that one should recognize that the normal sites you would use to check value (KBB, NADA etc.) or an inspection may not have a bearing on their bottom line price. Make your offer via phone and know they are firm at that number...no matter what. My suggestion, safe yourself a trip and buy elsewhere. There are plenty of better dealers out there.<//review>< pictures>
None</pictures>

<Date>1376190101998< /Date>< Rate>

< Text>
The banquet food at the Frog Bar & Grill is of very mixed quality. My sisters, brother, and I hosted an anniversary party for my parents at this lovely location and it appears that the quality control is non-existent. Also, the person in charge of organizing our event was hard to get a hold of and created some frustration for us. We had a pecan dessert served in a pastry fried in rancid or old oil, and the prime rib was the toughest I've ever had and others complained as well. One guest complained of feeling sick in the early morning hours following our event - likely the pecan dessert. The waitstaff was excellent, the location overlooking the Goleta Valley and ocean is beautiful, the creme brulee, salads were very good. I have also had lunch at the Frog Bar & Grill a number of times and have had a good experience. However, if you are bringing friends from out of town and having an important event, you are taking a risk.</Text>

<review>Beware of hidden fees when you rent from the leasing office. Regents La Jolla is the best community around UCSD, but there are two types of owners and renters need to consider the differences. The leasing office owns a lot of units in this complex. Please remember that on top of rent, renters need to pay for water, trash, sewer, etc if you deal with the leasing office. These fees vary each month, below is an example of the bill. You can see that the fees amount to $78. If you rent from individual owners, they only charge you rent (maybe plus water, but definitely no trash and sewer). So when compare the two prices, make sure that you'll pay more monthly if you rent from the leasing office. But I'm not saying that renting from the leasing office doesn't have advantage.  if you have problems with plumbing, appliances, etc, the leasing office will dispatch repair workers very soon (usually the same day) and if you rent from individual owner, you probably need to wait for a few days for the repair to be done. <rate>3<//rate>< Review>
Solid food with a nice view. Walking around La Jolla, it was difficult to find restaurants that we're still open at this time. This place was and had a few seats outside and we we're lucky enough to grab an open table. Tried the mahi mahi and shrimp tacos and some queso to start it off. Prices were a bit higher than the food quality, but it wasn't bad at all. Living in socal, I feel spoiled with authentic mexican food and comparing this place to places back home near LA didn't help my feeling toward it. Take this all with a grain of salt as you don't really get the full experience of a restaurant during covid. Food and drinks were fresh and tasty, just a bit forgettable.<//Review>

This is my one of my favorite places to grab a meal in La Jolla village that won't break the bank.  The atmosphere is lively and casual, much more casual than most other restaurants in the village.  The food is pretty standard Mexican comfort fare, but it's solid and the service is friendly and consistent.  This is a great place to bring a group of friends for relatively cheap eats in La Jolla.< /review>

<user_id>114185998177775225250< /user_id>< text>
Totally unexpected gem. The heat margarita was deilicous, spicy yet flavorful. I wanted to offer everything on the menu so my fiancee and I decided to split whatever we ordered. He got the CA burrito, I don't usually like CA burritos, but this was the best burrito I've ever had. The fries were crispy inside, the guacamole abd sour cream were delicious, thwir carne asada is delicious, but their homemade tasting tortilla was the icing on the cake. I would recommend anything with their carne asada. It's lean, flavorful and juicy. We also got the fried mahi tacos which didn't disappoint, the yellow corn tortilla tastes homemade as well. Totally blown away by the quality of the food and it's not outrageous priced. Will be going here again for sure.<//text>
